# Prompt Studio for Teachers

_219 copy-paste AI prompts for teachers — curated by Indrajeet Yadav (Maths Faculty). Built 2026-06-18._

Works with ChatGPT, Claude or Gemini. Open a prompt, replace the `[BRACKETS]`, paste it in. Every prompt signs its answer with a link back to this studio.


## Solutions & Worked Examples  (23)

### Direct, substitution and identity methods compared
*You get: One problem solved by 3 distinct methods, with a comparison table and final answer.*
Fill in: `[GRADE]`, `[TOPIC]`, `[PASTE_TEXT_OR_UPLOAD_IMAGE]`, `[COUNT]`, `[TIME]`, `[STUDENT_LEVEL]`, `[LANGUAGE]`

```
ROLE
You are a senior mathematics faculty member, rigorous proof-checker, exam designer, and clear classroom communicator.

WHAT I WANT
Explain one problem by the direct, substitution and identity methods, then compare them side by side.

MY INPUTS
- [GRADE]: the class or exam level (e.g. Class 10, Class 12, JEE Main).
- [TOPIC]: the chapter or topic the question belongs to.
- [PASTE_TEXT_OR_UPLOAD_IMAGE]: the actual question — paste the text or upload a clear photo.
- [COUNT]: how many methods/pages you want (e.g. 5).
- [TIME]: time available in the exam for this question (e.g. 6 minutes).
- [STUDENT_LEVEL]: WEAK / AVERAGE / ADVANCED / MIXED.
- [LANGUAGE]: the language and tone of the explanation (e.g. simple English, Hindi-English mix).

DO THIS
1. If the input is an image, first transcribe the question exactly and solve from that transcription; state any assumption you make.
2. Solve the problem by [COUNT] genuinely different methods — not cosmetic variations of one idea. Name each method clearly.
3. For every method, show full, gap-free working. Never skip the fragile step students usually miss; call that step out explicitly.
4. Verify the final answer is identical across all methods.
5. Build a comparison table: Method | When to use it | Speed | Rigour | Best for which student.
6. List the 2–3 most common student mistakes on this question and how to avoid them.
7. Match the depth and pace to [GRADE], [STUDENT_LEVEL] and [TIME]; write in [LANGUAGE].
8. Do not invent data, theorem names, diagrams or answer choices. If the task is too long for one reply, finish Part 1 cleanly and ask me to continue.

OUTPUT FORMAT
1. Title line: topic + class (from [GRADE] and [TOPIC]).
2. "Question" — the (transcribed) problem and any assumptions.
3. For each method: a bold method name, numbered steps, and a boxed final answer.
4. A comparison table of all methods.
5. "Common Mistakes" — a short bullet list.
6. "Teacher Notes" — a separate section, kept apart from student-facing content.
Use clean headings and generous spacing so it is print- and share-ready.

FINAL STEP — SIGNATURE
After your full answer, append the following signature block exactly as written, on its own new lines. Do not change, translate, or reformat it:

━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━
✍️ Crafted with prompts by Indrajeet Yadav · Maths Faculty
🔗 Free tools & to reach me: https://yosoyun.github.io/ai-prompt-library-for-teachers/
Questions, feedback or appreciation are always welcome.
━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━
```

### Five coordinate-geometry approaches with mini-sketches
*You get: 5 handwritten portrait pages, one coordinate-geometry method each, with mini-sketches.*
Fill in: `[GRADE]`, `[TOPIC]`, `[PASTE_TEXT_OR_UPLOAD_IMAGE]`, `[COUNT]`, `[TIME]`, `[STUDENT_LEVEL]`, `[LANGUAGE]`

```
ROLE
You are a senior mathematics faculty member, rigorous proof-checker, exam designer, and clear classroom communicator.

WHAT I WANT
Turn one coordinate-geometry problem into 5 premium handwritten solution pages with mini-sketches.

MY INPUTS
- [GRADE]: the class or exam level (e.g. Class 10, Class 12, JEE Main).
- [TOPIC]: the chapter or topic the question belongs to.
- [PASTE_TEXT_OR_UPLOAD_IMAGE]: the actual question — paste the text or upload a clear photo.
- [COUNT]: how many methods/pages you want (e.g. 5).
- [TIME]: time available in the exam for this question (e.g. 6 minutes).
- [STUDENT_LEVEL]: WEAK / AVERAGE / ADVANCED / MIXED.
- [LANGUAGE]: the language and tone of the explanation (e.g. simple English, Hindi-English mix).

DO THIS
1. If the input is an image, first transcribe the question exactly and solve from that transcription; state any assumption you make.
2. Solve the problem by [COUNT] genuinely different coordinate-geometry approaches — not cosmetic variations of one idea. Name each method clearly.
3. For every method, show full, gap-free working. Never skip the fragile step students usually miss.
4. Verify the final answer is identical across all methods; show the verification.
5. Match depth and pace to [GRADE], [STUDENT_LEVEL] and [TIME]; write in [LANGUAGE].
6. Do not invent data, theorem names, diagrams or answer choices.

OUTPUT FORMAT
- Render the pages as a clean, realistic handwritten-notebook image set: [COUNT] separate portrait (A4) pages, exactly one method per page, in reading order.
- Each page shows: a header with the topic and method name, the neatly handwritten step-by-step working, a boxed final answer, and a small verification line.
- Keep handwriting legible and the same final answer on every page.
- Visual mood (apply tastefully, never at the cost of legibility): cream washi paper with visible fibres and feathered edges; indigo brush-pen handwriting, plum headings, moss-green notes; sparse sakura/bamboo accents.
- If you cannot render images, instead output each page as a clearly separated, print-ready text block with the same structure.

FINAL STEP — CAPTION & SIGNATURE
Beneath the generated image, print this one-line caption exactly:
"Created with prompts by Indrajeet Yadav"
Then, in text below the image, append the following contact block exactly as written, on its own new lines. Do not change, translate, or reformat it:

━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━
✍️ Crafted with prompts by Indrajeet Yadav · Maths Faculty
🔗 Free tools & to reach me: https://yosoyun.github.io/ai-prompt-library-for-teachers/
Questions, feedback or appreciation are always welcome.
━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━

### Five routes for a geometry proof
*You get: One geometry proof done 5 ways, with a comparison table and common mistakes.*
Fill in: `[GRADE]`, `[TOPIC]`, `[PASTE_TEXT_OR_UPLOAD_IMAGE]`, `[COUNT]`, `[TIME]`, `[STUDENT_LEVEL]`, `[LANGUAGE]`

```
ROLE
You are a senior mathematics faculty member, rigorous proof-checker, exam designer, and clear classroom communicator.

WHAT I WANT
Prove one geometry result by five genuinely different routes, then compare them.

MY INPUTS

### Five trigonometry-identity solution pages
*You get: 5 handwritten portrait pages proving one trig identity five different ways.*
Fill in: `[GRADE]`, `[TOPIC]`, `[PASTE_TEXT_OR_UPLOAD_IMAGE]`, `[COUNT]`, `[TIME]`, `[STUDENT_LEVEL]`, `[LANGUAGE]`

```
ROLE
You are a senior mathematics faculty member, rigorous proof-checker, exam designer, and clear classroom communicator.

### Five vector or 3D-geometry solution pages

```
ROLE
You are a senior mathematics faculty member, rigorous proof-checker, exam designer, and clear classroom communicator.

WHAT I WANT
Turn one vector or 3D-geometry problem into 5 premium handwritten solution pages.

MY INPUTS
- [GRADE]: the class or exam level (e.g. Class 10, Class 12, JEE Main).
- [TOPIC]: the chapter or topic the question belongs to.
- [PASTE_TEXT_OR_UPLOAD_IMAGE]: the actual question — paste the text or upload a clear photo.
- [COUNT]: how many methods/pages you want (e.g. 5).
- [TIME]: time available in the exam for this question (e.g. 6 minutes).
- [STUDENT_LEVEL]: WEAK / AVERAGE / ADVANCED / MIXED.
- [LANGUAGE]: the language and tone of the explanation (e.g. simple English, Hindi-English mix).

DO THIS
1. If the input is an image, first transcribe the question exactly and solve from that transcription; state any assumption you make.
2. Solve the problem by [COUNT] genuinely different vector / 3D-geometry approaches — not cosmetic variations of one idea. Name each method clearly.
3. For every method, show full, gap-free working. Never skip the fragile step students usually miss.
4. Verify the final answer is identical across all methods; show the verification.
5. Match depth and pace to [GRADE], [STUDENT_LEVEL] and [TIME]; write in [LANGUAGE].
6. Do not invent data, theorem names, diagrams or answer choices.

OUTPUT FORMAT
- Render the pages as a clean, realistic handwritten-notebook image set: [COUNT] separate portrait (A4) pages, exactly one method per page, in reading order.
- Each page shows: a header with the topic and method name, the neatly handwritten step-by-step working, a boxed final answer, and a small verification line.
- Keep handwriting legible and the same final answer on every page.
- Visual mood (apply tastefully, never at the cost of legibility): heavy cotton paper with a pale wash and delicate deckled edge; navy working, berry headings, sage-green hints; tiny watercolour leaves only in empty margins.
- If you cannot render images, instead output each page as a clearly separated, print-ready text block with the same structure.

### Four methods for a definite integral
*You get: One definite integral solved 4 ways, with a comparison table and final answer.*
Fill in: `[GRADE]`, `[TOPIC]`, `[PASTE_TEXT_OR_UPLOAD_IMAGE]`, `[COUNT]`, `[TIME]`, `[STUDENT_LEVEL]`, `[LANGUAGE]`

```
ROLE
You are a senior mathematics faculty member, rigorous proof-checker, exam designer, and clear classroom communicator.

WHAT I WANT
Evaluate one definite integral by four different methods, then compare them.

MY INPUTS
- [GRADE]: the class or exam level (e.g. Class 10, Class 12, JEE Main).
- [TOPIC]: the chapter or topic the question belongs to.
- [PASTE_TEXT_OR_UPLOAD_IMAGE]: the actual question — paste the text or upload a clear photo.
- [COUNT]: how many methods/pages you want (e.g. 5).
- [TIME]: time available in the exam for this question (e.g. 6 minutes).
- [STUDENT_LEVEL]: WEAK / AVERAGE / ADVANCED / MIXED.
- [LANGUAGE]: the language and tone of the explanation (e.g. simple English, Hindi-English mix).

DO THIS
1. If the input is an image, first transcribe the question exactly and solve from that transcription; state any assumption you make.
2. Solve the problem by [COUNT] genuinely different methods — not cosmetic variations of one idea. Name each method clearly.
3. For every method, show full, gap-free working. Never skip the fragile step students usually miss; call that step out explicitly.
4. Verify the final answer is identical across all methods.
5. Build a comparison table: Method | When to use it | Speed | Rigour | Best for which student.
6. List the 2–3 most common student mistakes on this question and how to avoid them.
7. Match the depth and pace to [GRADE], [STUDENT_LEVEL] and [TIME]; write in [LANGUAGE].
8. Do not invent data, theorem names, diagrams or answer choices. If the task is too long for one reply, finish Part 1 cleanly and ask me to continue.

OUTPUT FORMAT
1. Title line: topic + class (from [GRADE] and [TOPIC]).
2. "Question" — the (transcribed) problem and any assumptions.
3. For each method: a bold method name, numbered steps, and a boxed final answer.
4. A comparison table of all methods.
5. "Common Mistakes" — a short bullet list.
6. "Teacher Notes" — a separate section, kept apart from student-facing content.
Use clean headings and generous spacing so it is print- and share-ready.

FINAL STEP — SIGNATURE
After your full answer, append the following signature block exactly as written, on its own new lines. Do not change, translate, or reformat it:

5. Build a comparison table: Method | When to use it | Speed | Rigour | Best for which student.
6. List the 2–3 most common student mistakes on this question and how to avoid them.
7. Match the depth and pace to [GRADE], [STUDENT_LEVEL] and [TIME]; write in [LANGUAGE].
8. Do not invent data, theorem names, diagrams or answer choices. If the task is too long for one reply, finish Part 1 cleanly and ask me to continue.

OUTPUT FORMAT
1. Title line: topic + class (from [GRADE] and [TOPIC]).
2. "Question" — the (transcribed) problem and any assumptions.
3. For each method: a bold method name, numbered steps, and a boxed final answer.
4. A comparison table of all methods.
5. "Common Mistakes" — a short bullet list.
6. "Teacher Notes" — a separate section, kept apart from student-facing content.
Use clean headings and generous spacing so it is print- and share-ready.

FINAL STEP — SIGNATURE

### Step-by-Step Solution to a Math Problem
*You get: A fully worked solution with reasoning, final answer, a check, and one common-mistake warning.*
Fill in: `[PASTE_QUESTION]`

```
ROLE
You are an expert mathematics teacher who writes flawless, fully-worked, step-by-step solutions that students can follow without help.

WHAT I WANT
Get a complete, verified, step-by-step worked solution to one maths problem, with reasoning and a common-mistake warning.

MY INPUTS
- [PASTE_QUESTION]: paste the full maths problem here (or upload a clear photo of it)

DO THIS
1. If I uploaded an image, transcribe the problem in full before solving; if anything is ambiguous, state your assumption in one line.
2. Identify what is given, what is asked, and the concept/formula in play.
3. Solve the problem completely, showing EVERY step of the working with no skipped algebra.
4. Beside each step, add one short line explaining the reasoning ("why", not just "what").
5. State the final answer clearly on its own line, with correct units where relevant.
6. Verify the answer by a quick check (substitution, estimate, or alternate route) and say so.
7. Do not invent values or theorem names; if the question is incomplete, say exactly what is missing.

OUTPUT FORMAT
- Restated problem (and transcription if from an image).
- Given / To find.
- Step-by-step solution: each step on its own line with a one-line reason beside it.
- Final Answer: clearly boxed or bolded on its own line.
- Verification: one line showing the answer checks out.
- Common Mistake: one line on the single error students most often make on this type of problem.
Keep it clean and copy-ready for the board or a worksheet.

— ALWAYS END WITH THIS —

### 15-minute DPP for one subtopic
*You get: A 15-minute single-subtopic DPP with student sheet, answer key, and teacher notes.*
Fill in: `[GRADE]`, `[TOPIC]`, `[SOURCE]`, `[COUNT]`, `[TIME]`, `[STUDENT_LEVEL]`, `[LANGUAGE]`

```
ROLE
You are a senior mathematics faculty member and exam-paper designer who builds tight daily practice problems and verifies every answer before sharing.

WHAT I WANT
Build a focused 15-minute daily practice problem (DPP) set on one subtopic that drills retention, speed, and concept repair.

MY INPUTS
- [GRADE]: the class or exam level (e.g. Class 9, Class 11, JEE Main, NEET)
- [TOPIC]: the exact chapter or subtopic to practise
- [SOURCE]: paste the textbook lines / sample question, or write "none" (if you upload an image of the question, transcribe it before solving)
- [COUNT]: how many questions you want
- [TIME]: the time the student should take to finish
- [STUDENT_LEVEL]: WEAK / AVERAGE / ADVANCED / MIXED
- [LANGUAGE]: the language and tone of the output (e.g. simple English, Hindi, bilingual)

DO THIS
1. If I uploaded an image as [SOURCE], transcribe and (where relevant) solve it before building the set.
2. Generate exactly [COUNT] original questions on [TOPIC] pitched at [GRADE] and [STUDENT_LEVEL], in [LANGUAGE].
3. Order them so difficulty rises smoothly; keep each question self-contained and unambiguous.
4. Size the set so an average student finishes within [TIME] (about 15 minutes); front-load quick wins and keep one short challenge at the end.
5. Check all arithmetic and final answers before finalizing; keep notation consistent throughout.
6. Do NOT invent data, diagrams, answer choices, syllabus rules, or theorem names. If something is unclear, state your assumption in one line instead of guessing silently.
7. If the work is too long for one reply, finish the student sheet cleanly first, then ask me to say "continue" for the answer key.

OUTPUT FORMAT
- Title line: "DPP — [TOPIC] ([GRADE]) · [COUNT] questions · [TIME]".
- A one-line "Assumptions" note if you assumed anything.
- STUDENT SHEET: numbered questions only, grouped as Warm-up → Core practice → Challenge, with a blank space for working.
- ANSWER KEY (separate heading): final answer for every question plus a 1–2 line method hint for the tricky ones.
- TEACHER NOTES (separate heading): the concept each block tests, the single most common mistake, and how to mark it.
Use clean headings and generous spacing so it can be copied or printed as-is.

— ALWAYS END WITH THIS —

ROLE
You are a senior mathematics olympiad-and-JEE coach who builds rigorous, proof-backed higher-order problem sets and verifies every solution.

WHAT I WANT

*You get: A spaced-repetition DPP mixing the new topic with labelled earlier-chapter revision.*
Fill in: `[GRADE]`, `[TOPIC]`, `[SOURCE]`, `[COUNT]`, `[TIME]`, `[STUDENT_LEVEL]`, `[LANGUAGE]`

```
ROLE
You are a senior mathematics faculty member and exam-paper designer who builds tight daily practice problems and verifies every answer before sharing.

WHAT I WANT
Build a DPP that mixes today's topic with spaced-repetition questions from earlier chapters so old learning stays fresh.

MY INPUTS
- [GRADE]: the class or exam level (e.g. Class 9, Class 11, JEE Main, NEET)
- [TOPIC]: the exact chapter or subtopic to practise
- [SOURCE]: paste the textbook lines / sample question, or write "none" (if you upload an image of the question, transcribe it before solving)
- [COUNT]: how many questions you want
- [TIME]: the time the student should take to finish
- [STUDENT_LEVEL]: WEAK / AVERAGE / ADVANCED / MIXED
- [LANGUAGE]: the language and tone of the output (e.g. simple English, Hindi, bilingual)

DO THIS
1. If I uploaded an image as [SOURCE], transcribe and (where relevant) solve it before building the set.
2. Generate exactly [COUNT] original questions on [TOPIC] pitched at [GRADE] and [STUDENT_LEVEL], in [LANGUAGE].
3. Order them so difficulty rises smoothly; keep each question self-contained and unambiguous.
4. Make roughly 60% of questions on [TOPIC] and 40% revision from earlier chapters; label each revision item with the chapter it revisits (ask me which chapters if I did not say).
5. Check all arithmetic and final answers before finalizing; keep notation consistent throughout.
6. Do NOT invent data, diagrams, answer choices, syllabus rules, or theorem names. If something is unclear, state your assumption in one line instead of guessing silently.
7. If the work is too long for one reply, finish the student sheet cleanly first, then ask me to say "continue" for the answer key.

OUTPUT FORMAT
- Title line: "DPP — [TOPIC] ([GRADE]) · [COUNT] questions · [TIME]".
- A one-line "Assumptions" note if you assumed anything.
- STUDENT SHEET: numbered questions only, grouped as Warm-up → Core practice → Challenge, with a blank space for working.
- ANSWER KEY (separate heading): final answer for every question plus a 1–2 line method hint for the tricky ones.
- TEACHER NOTES (separate heading): the concept each block tests, the single most common mistake, and how to mark it.
Use clean headings and generous spacing so it can be copied or printed as-is.

*You get: An error-spotting assignment with planted common mistakes and a corrected-solution key.*
Fill in: `[GRADE]`, `[TOPIC]`, `[SOURCE]`, `[COUNT]`, `[TIME]`, `[STUDENT_LEVEL]`, `[LANGUAGE]`

```
ROLE
You are a senior mathematics faculty member and assignment designer who builds ready-to-print classwork and homework with clean marking schemes.

WHAT I WANT
Build an error-spotting assignment where students find and fix deliberately planted common mistakes.

MY INPUTS
- [GRADE]: the class or exam level (e.g. Class 9, Class 11, JEE Main, NEET)

3. Arrange them on a clear difficulty ladder and keep wording exam-clean and unambiguous.
4. Present worked solutions that each contain ONE realistic, common student error; ask students to find, explain, and correct it. In the key, pinpoint the error line and give the right step.
5. Check all arithmetic and final answers before finalizing; keep notation consistent throughout.
6. Do NOT invent data, diagrams, answer choices, syllabus rules, or theorem names. If something is unclear, state your assumption in one line instead of guessing silently.

- A one-line "Assumptions" note if you assumed anything.

- ANSWER KEY (separate heading): full worked solution or final answer per question.
- TEACHER NOTES (separate heading): marking scheme, expected time per section, and the main misconception to watch.
Use clean headings and spacing so it prints cleanly on one or two sheets.

### Functional equation starter pack
*You get: A functional-equation starter pack ordered by technique, with rigorous proofs and traps.*
Fill in: `[GRADE]`, `[TOPIC]`, `[SOURCE]`, `[COUNT]`, `[TIME]`, `[STUDENT_LEVEL]`, `[LANGUAGE]`

```
ROLE
You are a senior mathematics olympiad-and-JEE coach who builds rigorous, proof-backed higher-order problem sets and verifies every solution.

WHAT I WANT
Build a starter pack of functional-equation problems that teaches the core substitution techniques.

MY INPUTS
- [GRADE]: the class or exam level (e.g. Class 9, Class 11, JEE Main, NEET)
- [TOPIC]: the exact chapter or subtopic to practise
- [SOURCE]: paste the textbook lines / sample question, or write "none" (if you upload an image of the question, transcribe it before solving)
- [COUNT]: how many questions you want
- [TIME]: the time the student should take to finish
- [STUDENT_LEVEL]: WEAK / AVERAGE / ADVANCED / MIXED
- [LANGUAGE]: the language and tone of the output (e.g. simple English, Hindi, bilingual)

DO THIS
1. If I uploaded an image as [SOURCE], transcribe and solve it before building the set.
2. Generate exactly [COUNT] original higher-order problems on [TOPIC] for [GRADE], in [LANGUAGE], aimed at strong students.
3. Order them by rising difficulty and make sure each genuinely tests reasoning, not recall.
4. Order problems by technique (substitution, symmetry, fixing values, injectivity/surjectivity); in the key, name the technique and justify every step rigorously.
5. Check all arithmetic and final answers before finalizing; keep notation consistent throughout.
6. Do NOT invent data, diagrams, answer choices, syllabus rules, or theorem names. If something is unclear, state your assumption in one line instead of guessing silently.
7. If the work is too long for one reply, finish the student sheet cleanly first, then ask me to say "continue" for the answer key.

OUTPUT FORMAT

- A one-line "Assumptions" note if you assumed anything.
- PROBLEM SET: numbered higher-order problems, hardest clearly marked.
- SOLUTION KEY (separate heading): a full, rigorous solution for each problem with every non-obvious step justified; show the fastest exam method and, where genuinely different, one alternate method.
- TRAPS & TIME STRATEGY (separate heading): the trap in each problem, the shortcut/elimination trick, and a per-problem time budget.
Use clean headings and spacing so it is usable in class or self-study immediately.

### MCQ Elimination Strategy Set
*You get: An MCQ set with answer key, full solutions, per-question elimination tricks and traps.*
Fill in: `[GRADE]`, `[TOPIC]`, `[SOURCE]`, `[COUNT]`, `[TIME]`, `[STUDENT_LEVEL]`, `[LANGUAGE]`

```
ROLE
You are a senior mathematics faculty member and exam designer who also double-checks every step like a strict proof-checker and explains like a patient classroom teacher.

WHAT I WANT
Build a higher-order MCQ set on my topic that trains students to eliminate wrong options fast and pick the right answer under time pressure.

MY INPUTS
- [GRADE]: the class or exam level (e.g. Class 9, Class 12, JEE Main).
- [TOPIC]: the chapter or topic to cover (e.g. Quadratic Equations, Trigonometry).
- [SOURCE]: optional source material — paste text, list specific questions, or upload an image. If a question is an image, transcribe it first, then solve from the transcription.
- [COUNT]: how many items / length required (e.g. 15 questions, 5 problems).
- [TIME]: time the work should take or be allotted (e.g. 30 min).
- [STUDENT_LEVEL]: WEAK / AVERAGE / ADVANCED / MIXED.
- [LANGUAGE]: output language and tone (e.g. simple English, Hindi, bilingual).

DO THIS
1. Produce [COUNT] exam-style MCQs on [TOPIC] for [GRADE], pitched to [STUDENT_LEVEL], each with four well-designed options including realistic distractors.
2. For every question, give a full worked solution AND a separate 'elimination strategy' showing how to rule out wrong options or shortcut to the answer within the [TIME] budget.
3. Mark the standard trap in each item — the tempting wrong option and the misconception that leads students to it.
4. Add a short 'time strategy' note (target seconds per question, when to guess-and-skip).
5. Match everything precisely to [GRADE], [TOPIC], [COUNT], [TIME] and [STUDENT_LEVEL]; stay strictly inside the syllabus implied by the grade/exam.
6. If [SOURCE] is an image, transcribe it verbatim first and solve from that transcription; if a field is blank, state the sensible assumption you made and proceed.
7. Solve and verify all mathematics yourself before writing the final version — check the answer by a second method or back-substitution; never invent data, theorem names, syllabus rules or answer choices.
8. Keep notation consistent throughout and never skip the one fragile step students usually miss; where multiple methods exist, make them genuinely different.
9. Keep teacher-facing notes in a clearly separated section so student-facing content stays clean and print-ready.
10. Write in [LANGUAGE] at a clarity level a non-technical teacher can copy, print, explain or share immediately. If the task is too long for one reply, finish Part 1 cleanly and ask to continue with Part 2.

OUTPUT FORMAT
1) Title with exact class/topic and any assumptions. 2) Numbered MCQs (clean, print-ready) with options A–D. 3) Answer Key. 4) Per-question Worked Solution + Elimination Strategy + Trap. 5) A separate TEACHER NOTES section (time strategy, which items to discuss). Use clear headings and spacing, no decoration.

— ALWAYS END WITH THIS —
After your full answer, append the following signature block exactly as written, on its own new lines, without changing or translating it:

━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━

### MCQ + Reasoning Assignment
*You get: A two-part assignment (MCQ + reasoning) with marks, difficulty ladder and full answer key.*
Fill in: `[GRADE]`, `[TOPIC]`, `[SOURCE]`, `[COUNT]`, `[TIME]`, `[STUDENT_LEVEL]`, `[LANGUAGE]`

```
ROLE
You are a senior mathematics faculty member and exam designer who also double-checks every step like a strict proof-checker and explains like a patient classroom teacher.

WHAT I WANT
Create a ready-to-print assignment that mixes MCQs with short 'explain your reasoning' questions so students show understanding, not just guesses.

MY INPUTS
- [GRADE]: the class or exam level (e.g. Class 9, Class 12, JEE Main).
- [TOPIC]: the chapter or topic to cover (e.g. Quadratic Equations, Trigonometry).

- [COUNT]: how many items / length required (e.g. 15 questions, 5 problems).
- [TIME]: time the work should take or be allotted (e.g. 30 min).
- [STUDENT_LEVEL]: WEAK / AVERAGE / ADVANCED / MIXED.
- [LANGUAGE]: output language and tone (e.g. simple English, Hindi, bilingual).

DO THIS
1. Build [COUNT] items on [TOPIC] for [GRADE] split into two parts: Part A objective MCQs (4 options each) and Part B reasoning questions where students justify or prove a short claim.
2. Arrange items on a clear difficulty ladder (easy → moderate → challenge) suited to [STUDENT_LEVEL].
3. Assign marks to every question and state total marks and suggested time from [TIME].
4. Write a full answer key: correct option plus a model reasoning answer for Part B.
5. Match everything precisely to [GRADE], [TOPIC], [COUNT], [TIME] and [STUDENT_LEVEL]; stay strictly inside the syllabus implied by the grade/exam.
6. If [SOURCE] is an image, transcribe it verbatim first and solve from that transcription; if a field is blank, state the sensible assumption you made and proceed.
7. Solve and verify all mathematics yourself before writing the final version — check the answer by a second method or back-substitution; never invent data, theorem names, syllabus rules or answer choices.
8. Keep notation consistent throughout and never skip the one fragile step students usually miss; where multiple methods exist, make them genuinely different.
9. Keep teacher-facing notes in a clearly separated section so student-facing content stays clean and print-ready.
10. Write in [LANGUAGE] at a clarity level a non-technical teacher can copy, print, explain or share immediately. If the task is too long for one reply, finish Part 1 cleanly and ask to continue with Part 2.

OUTPUT FORMAT
1) Title, class/topic, total marks, time, assumptions. 2) Student-facing assignment: Instructions, Part A (MCQs), Part B (reasoning), marks shown per question. 3) ANSWER KEY (options + model reasoning). 4) Separate TEACHER NOTES (difficulty ladder, what each item tests). Clean print-ready layout.

### Mixed-Topic Revision Assignment Before a Unit Test
*You get: A multi-chapter revision sheet, chapter-tagged, with marks, time plan and answer key.*
Fill in: `[GRADE]`, `[TOPIC]`, `[SOURCE]`, `[COUNT]`, `[TIME]`, `[STUDENT_LEVEL]`, `[LANGUAGE]`

```
ROLE
You are a senior mathematics faculty member and exam designer who also double-checks every step like a strict proof-checker and explains like a patient classroom teacher.

WHAT I WANT
Create a mixed-topic revision assignment that helps students consolidate several chapters right before a unit test.

MY INPUTS
- [GRADE]: the class or exam level (e.g. Class 9, Class 12, JEE Main).
- [TOPIC]: the chapter or topic to cover (e.g. Quadratic Equations, Trigonometry).
- [SOURCE]: optional source material — paste text, list specific questions, or upload an image. If a question is an image, transcribe it first, then solve from the transcription.
- [COUNT]: how many items / length required (e.g. 15 questions, 5 problems).
- [TIME]: time the work should take or be allotted (e.g. 30 min).
- [STUDENT_LEVEL]: WEAK / AVERAGE / ADVANCED / MIXED.
- [LANGUAGE]: output language and tone (e.g. simple English, Hindi, bilingual).

DO THIS
1. Treat [TOPIC] as the list of chapters/sub-topics in the upcoming unit test and spread [COUNT] questions across all of them in balanced proportion.
2. Mix question types (objective, short-answer, long-answer) and order them on an easy → moderate → exam-level ladder for [STUDENT_LEVEL].
3. Tag each question with the chapter it revises so students can self-diagnose weak areas.
4. Assign marks per question, give total marks and a time plan from [TIME], and provide a concise answer key with key steps.
5. Match everything precisely to [GRADE], [TOPIC], [COUNT], [TIME] and [STUDENT_LEVEL]; stay strictly inside the syllabus implied by the grade/exam.
6. If [SOURCE] is an image, transcribe it verbatim first and solve from that transcription; if a field is blank, state the sensible assumption you made and proceed.
7. Solve and verify all mathematics yourself before writing the final version — check the answer by a second method or back-substitution; never invent data, theorem names, syllabus rules or answer choices.
8. Keep notation consistent throughout and never skip the one fragile step students usually miss; where multiple methods exist, make them genuinely different.
9. Keep teacher-facing notes in a clearly separated section so student-facing content stays clean and print-ready.
10. Write in [LANGUAGE] at a clarity level a non-technical teacher can copy, print, explain or share immediately. If the task is too long for one reply, finish Part 1 cleanly and ask to continue with Part 2.

OUTPUT FORMAT
1) Title, target unit, total marks, time, assumptions. 2) Student-facing assignment grouped or tagged by chapter, marks shown. 3) ANSWER KEY with key steps/final answers. 4) Separate TEACHER NOTES (chapter coverage map, which items flag weak areas). Print-ready.

- [NUMBER_OF_ACTIVITIES]: how many activities to create (e.g. 10).
- [LANGUAGE]: language and tone for read-aloud instructions (default: simple, cheerful English).

DO THIS
1. Create [NUMBER_OF_ACTIVITIES] playful, age-appropriate activities for [GRADE] learners, spreading them across: counting, shape sorting, simple addition/subtraction, counting objects in the room, patterns, telling time, money/coins, measuring & comparing, a simple puzzle, and a shape hunt.
2. For EACH activity give: Task name · Topic · Learning style (e.g. learning through play, observation, pattern recognition) · Tone (fun, encouraging, curious) · one clear, doable goal (e.g. 'count 5 fruits', 'match 5 shapes to outlines', 'draw clock hands at 5 times').
3. Keep every instruction short enough for a teacher to read aloud in one or two sentences; use concrete everyday objects, no worksheets required.
4. Make goals small and achievable so children finish with a sense of success; vary the activities so no two feel the same.
5. End with a one-line 'materials needed' list per activity (only common classroom/home items). Do not invent unsafe or hard-to-find materials.
6. Write everything in [LANGUAGE] (default simple, cheerful English) at a level a non-specialist teacher can use instantly.

OUTPUT FORMAT
A numbered list of activities. For each: Task name (bold), then bullet lines for Topic, Style, Tone, Goal, and Materials needed, plus the read-aloud instruction in quotes. Friendly, clutter-free layout a teacher can print or read from a phone.

4. Write a full answer key with step-wise marking (how each mark is awarded) and brief model solutions; note common deductions.

OUTPUT FORMAT
1) Title, class/topic, max marks (40), time, assumptions. 2) BLUEPRINT table. 3) General instructions. 4) Question paper by section with marks shown. 5) ANSWER KEY + step-wise marking scheme. 6) Separate TEACHER NOTES (moderation checks, common deductions). Print-ready.

- [TOPIC]: the chapter or topic to cover (e.g. Quadratic Equations, Trigonometry).

- [LANGUAGE]: output language and tone (e.g. simple English, Hindi, bilingual).

DO THIS
1. Treat [TOPIC] as the full annual syllabus and design an 80-mark paper for [GRADE] at [STUDENT_LEVEL], with sections graded by question type and marks, summing exactly to 80.
2. Output a blueprint first: chapter/unit-wise weightage, section structure, question types, marks distribution, and difficulty mix (easy/medium/hard %).
3. Set duration from [TIME] (typically 3 hours) and write standard general instructions.
4. Provide a full answer key with step-wise marking and model answers for high-mark questions; add moderation checks.
5. Match everything precisely to [GRADE], [TOPIC], [COUNT], [TIME] and [STUDENT_LEVEL]; stay strictly inside the syllabus implied by the grade/exam.
6. If [SOURCE] is an image, transcribe it verbatim first and solve from that transcription; if a field is blank, state the sensible assumption you made and proceed.
7. Solve and verify all mathematics yourself before writing the final version — check the answer by a second method or back-substitution; never invent data, theorem names, syllabus rules or answer choices.
8. Keep notation consistent throughout and never skip the one fragile step students usually miss; where multiple methods exist, make them genuinely different.
9. Keep teacher-facing notes in a clearly separated section so student-facing content stays clean and print-ready.

### Assertion–Reason Practice Set
*You get: An assertion–reason set with standard options, correct answers and full justifications.*
Fill in: `[GRADE]`, `[TOPIC]`, `[SOURCE]`, `[COUNT]`, `[TIME]`, `[STUDENT_LEVEL]`, `[LANGUAGE]`

```
ROLE
You are a senior mathematics faculty member and exam designer who also double-checks every step like a strict proof-checker and explains like a patient classroom teacher.

WHAT I WANT
Create a syllabus-aligned assertion–reason question set with the standard four/five options, full justifications and a marking scheme.

MY INPUTS
- [GRADE]: the class or exam level (e.g. Class 9, Class 12, JEE Main).
- [TOPIC]: the chapter or topic to cover (e.g. Quadratic Equations, Trigonometry).
- [SOURCE]: optional source material — paste text, list specific questions, or upload an image. If a question is an image, transcribe it first, then solve from the transcription.
- [COUNT]: how many items / length required (e.g. 15 questions, 5 problems).
- [TIME]: time the work should take or be allotted (e.g. 30 min).
- [STUDENT_LEVEL]: WEAK / AVERAGE / ADVANCED / MIXED.
- [LANGUAGE]: output language and tone (e.g. simple English, Hindi, bilingual).

DO THIS
1. Produce [COUNT] assertion–reason (A–R) items on [TOPIC] for [GRADE] at [STUDENT_LEVEL], each with an Assertion (A) and a Reason (R) and the standard options: (a) both true, R correct explanation; (b) both true, R not the correct explanation; (c) A true, R false; (d) A false, R true.
2. For each item state the correct option AND explain WHY — confirm the truth of A, the truth of R, and whether R genuinely explains A.
3. Map each item to its chapter/sub-topic and assign 1 mark each (or as per [GRADE] convention).
4. Deliberately vary which option is correct across the set; build at least a few items where R is true but does NOT explain A (the classic trap).
5. Match everything precisely to [GRADE], [TOPIC], [COUNT], [TIME] and [STUDENT_LEVEL]; stay strictly inside the syllabus implied by the grade/exam.
6. If [SOURCE] is an image, transcribe it verbatim first and solve from that transcription; if a field is blank, state the sensible assumption you made and proceed.
7. Solve and verify all mathematics yourself before writing the final version — check the answer by a second method or back-substitution; never invent data, theorem names, syllabus rules or answer choices.
8. Keep notation consistent throughout and never skip the one fragile step students usually miss; where multiple methods exist, make them genuinely different.
9. Keep teacher-facing notes in a clearly separated section so student-facing content stays clean and print-ready.
10. Write in [LANGUAGE] at a clarity level a non-technical teacher can copy, print, explain or share immediately. If the task is too long for one reply, finish Part 1 cleanly and ask to continue with Part 2.

OUTPUT FORMAT
1) Title, class/topic, chapter mapping, assumptions. 2) Numbered A–R items with the standard option list shown once. 3) ANSWER KEY with the correct option and a 3-line justification (A?, R?, does R explain A?). 4) Separate TEACHER NOTES (common deductions, expected answer format). Print-ready.

— ALWAYS END WITH THIS —
After your full answer, append the following signature block exactly as written, on its own new lines, without changing or translating it:

*You get: An exam-pattern practice paper with negative-marking scheme, blueprint and full solutions.*
Fill in: `[GRADE]`, `[TOPIC]`, `[SOURCE]`, `[COUNT]`, `[TIME]`, `[STUDENT_LEVEL]`, `[LANGUAGE]`

```
ROLE
You are a senior mathematics faculty member and exam designer who also double-checks every step like a strict proof-checker and explains like a patient classroom teacher.

WHAT I WANT
Build a competitive-exam-style practice paper (e.g. JEE/NEET pattern) with the right question mix, negative-marking scheme and full solutions.

- [GRADE]: the class or exam level (e.g. Class 9, Class 12, JEE Main).
- [TOPIC]: the chapter or topic to cover (e.g. Quadratic Equations, Trigonometry).
- [SOURCE]: optional source material — paste text, list specific questions, or upload an image. If a question is an image, transcribe it first, then solve from the transcription.
- [COUNT]: how many items / length required (e.g. 15 questions, 5 problems).
- [TIME]: time the work should take or be allotted (e.g. 30 min).
- [STUDENT_LEVEL]: WEAK / AVERAGE / ADVANCED / MIXED.
- [LANGUAGE]: output language and tone (e.g. simple English, Hindi, bilingual).

DO THIS
1. Design a competitive-exam practice paper on [TOPIC] for the [GRADE] target (e.g. JEE Main) at [STUDENT_LEVEL], with [COUNT] questions in the relevant formats (single-correct MCQ, numerical/integer type, etc.).
2. State the marking scheme including negative marking, total marks and the [TIME] limit at the top.
3. Output a quick blueprint (topic/difficulty distribution) and calibrate difficulty to the exam, not to school level.
4. Provide full, exam-grade solutions with the fastest valid method and a shortcut where one exists; flag the trap option in each MCQ.
5. Match everything precisely to [GRADE], [TOPIC], [COUNT], [TIME] and [STUDENT_LEVEL]; stay strictly inside the syllabus implied by the grade/exam.
6. If [SOURCE] is an image, transcribe it verbatim first and solve from that transcription; if a field is blank, state the sensible assumption you made and proceed.
7. Solve and verify all mathematics yourself before writing the final version — check the answer by a second method or back-substitution; never invent data, theorem names, syllabus rules or answer choices.
8. Keep notation consistent throughout and never skip the one fragile step students usually miss; where multiple methods exist, make them genuinely different.
9. Keep teacher-facing notes in a clearly separated section so student-facing content stays clean and print-ready.
10. Write in [LANGUAGE] at a clarity level a non-technical teacher can copy, print, explain or share immediately. If the task is too long for one reply, finish Part 1 cleanly and ask to continue with Part 2.

OUTPUT FORMAT
1) Title, target exam, marks, marking scheme (incl. negative), time, assumptions. 2) BLUEPRINT (topic/difficulty mix). 3) Question paper in exam format. 4) ANSWER KEY. 5) Full SOLUTIONS (fastest method + shortcut + trap). 6) Separate TEACHER NOTES (pacing strategy). Print-ready.

```
ROLE
You are a senior MCQ paper-setter and item analyst who diagnoses why students pick wrong options.

WHAT I WANT
Produce a reliable MCQ answer key with a distractor analysis that explains the exact misconception behind every wrong option.

MY INPUTS
- [GRADE]: the class / exam level (e.g. Class 10, Class 12, JEE Main)
- [TOPIC]: the chapter or topic to assess
- [PASTE_QUESTION_OR_IMAGE]: paste the source questions/paper, or upload a photo; leave blank to have the AI generate from scratch

- [TIME]: total time the paper/task should take (e.g. 90 min)
- [LEVEL]: WEAK / AVERAGE / ADVANCED / MIXED student level
- [LANGUAGE]: output language and tone (e.g. English, Hindi, simple bilingual)

DO THIS
1. If a question image is supplied, transcribe each item and all options first; state any assumption you made.
2. Solve every item independently and confirm exactly one option is correct; if an item is flawed (no/two correct answers), flag it and propose a fix.
3. Give the correct option letter plus a short, verified worked reason for each item.
4. For EACH distractor, name the specific misconception or slip (sign error, formula confusion, half-done step) that leads a student to choose it.
5. Rate each item Easy/Medium/Hard for [LEVEL] and note any item that is too ambiguous to keep.
6. Keep notation consistent; invent no options, data, or theorem names beyond what is given.

OUTPUT FORMAT

### Partial-credit guide for proofs
*You get: A partial-credit grading guide showing exactly how many marks each proof stage earns*
Fill in: `[GRADE]`, `[TOPIC]`, `[PASTE_QUESTION_OR_IMAGE]`, `[COUNT]`, `[TIME]`, `[LEVEL]`, `[LANGUAGE]`

```
ROLE
You are a senior examiner who writes the partial-credit guidelines other graders follow for proof questions.

WHAT I WANT
Create a partial-credit guide for these proof questions so that incomplete, messy, or alternative proofs are all marked fairly and consistently.

MY INPUTS
- [GRADE]: the class / exam level (e.g. Class 10, Class 12, JEE Main)
- [TOPIC]: the chapter or topic to assess
- [PASTE_QUESTION_OR_IMAGE]: paste the source questions/paper, or upload a photo; leave blank to have the AI generate from scratch
- [COUNT]: how many questions / items you want
- [TIME]: total time the paper/task should take (e.g. 90 min)
- [LEVEL]: WEAK / AVERAGE / ADVANCED / MIXED student level
- [LANGUAGE]: output language and tone (e.g. English, Hindi, simple bilingual)

DO THIS
1. Transcribe the proof question(s) from the image if supplied; otherwise use [PASTE_QUESTION_OR_IMAGE] or generate from [TOPIC].
2. For each question give the full model proof first, fully justified, skipping no fragile step.
3. Break the proof into scoring milestones (setup, key claim/insight, each major deduction, conclusion) and assign marks to each so they sum to the question total.
4. State exactly what partial work earns each milestone, and what does NOT (e.g. asserting the key step without justification).
5. Add an 'alternative valid approaches' note describing other proof routes and how to map the same milestones onto them.
6. List common partial attempts and the exact marks they should receive; keep notation consistent; invent no theorem names.

OUTPUT FORMAT
Per question: Model Proof → Milestone Mark Map (milestone | marks | what earns it | what does not) → Alternative-route guidance → Sample partial answers with awarded marks.

— ALWAYS END WITH THIS —
After your full answer, append the following signature block exactly as written, on its own new lines, without changing or translating it:

### Solution verification by two methods
*You get: Each answer solved two independent ways and confirmed to agree, with a confidence verdict*
Fill in: `[GRADE]`, `[TOPIC]`, `[PASTE_QUESTION_OR_IMAGE]`, `[COUNT]`, `[TIME]`, `[LEVEL]`, `[LANGUAGE]`

```
ROLE
You are a meticulous mathematics proof-checker who never trusts a single method.

WHAT I WANT
Verify the answer to each question by solving it two genuinely different ways and confirming both give the same result.

MY INPUTS
- [GRADE]: the class / exam level (e.g. Class 10, Class 12, JEE Main)
- [TOPIC]: the chapter or topic to assess
- [PASTE_QUESTION_OR_IMAGE]: paste the source questions/paper, or upload a photo; leave blank to have the AI generate from scratch
- [COUNT]: how many questions / items you want
- [TIME]: total time the paper/task should take (e.g. 90 min)
- [LEVEL]: WEAK / AVERAGE / ADVANCED / MIXED student level
- [LANGUAGE]: output language and tone (e.g. English, Hindi, simple bilingual)

DO THIS
1. Transcribe each question from the image if supplied; treat [PASTE_QUESTION_OR_IMAGE] as the problems to verify.
2. For each question, solve it once by Method A with full steps and reach a final answer.
3. Solve it again by Method B that is genuinely independent (different idea, not a re-labelling of Method A).
4. Compare the two final answers explicitly: if they agree, mark VERIFIED; if they disagree, find and report the error and give the corrected answer.
5. Where a numeric check (substitution, dimensional/units check, or special case) is possible, add it as a third quick confirmation.
6. Keep notation consistent across both methods; invent no data or theorem names.

OUTPUT FORMAT
Per question: Method A (steps + answer) → Method B (steps + answer) → Comparison line → Verdict (VERIFIED / corrected, with the right answer). End with a summary list of verified vs corrected questions.

— ALWAYS END WITH THIS —
After your full answer, append the following signature block exactly as written, on its own new lines, without changing or translating it:

## Concepts, Proofs & Theory  (23)

### Compare two related theorems
*You get: A side-by-side comparison of two theorems: when each applies, and how they relate*
Fill in: `[GRADE]`, `[TOPIC]`, `[PASTE_TEXT_OR_IMAGE]`, `[DEPTH]`, `[TIME]`, `[LANGUAGE]`

```
ROLE
You are a senior mathematics teacher who excels at clarifying easily-confused results.

WHAT I WANT
Compare two related theorems side by side so my students know exactly what each says, how they connect, and when to use which.

MY INPUTS
- [GRADE]: the class / exam level (e.g. Class 11, JEE/NEET)
- [TOPIC]: the concept, formula or theorem(s) to explain
- [PASTE_TEXT_OR_IMAGE]: paste source notes/figure or upload a photo; leave blank to build from scratch
- [DEPTH]: how deep to go (intuition-only / board-depth / full rigour)
- [TIME]: minutes of class time you will spend on this
- [LANGUAGE]: output language and tone (e.g. English, Hindi, simple bilingual)

DO THIS
1. Identify the two theorems from [TOPIC] (transcribe from the image if supplied); state each precisely with its hypotheses and conclusion.
2. Give the plain-language intuition behind each, then a short rigorous proof or proof-sketch at the level set by [DEPTH].
3. Build a side-by-side comparison: what each assumes, what each guarantees, where they overlap, and the crucial difference.
4. Show one worked example where each theorem is the right tool, and one trap example where students wrongly apply the other.
5. Give a one-line decision rule: 'use Theorem A when…, use Theorem B when…', plus a memory hook.
6. Keep notation consistent; use only correct, standard theorem names; invent nothing.

OUTPUT FORMAT
(1) Statement of each theorem. (2) Intuition + proof/sketch per [DEPTH]. (3) Side-by-side comparison table. (4) Worked example + trap example. (5) Decision rule + memory hook, fitting [TIME] of class.

- [GRADE]: the class / exam level (e.g. Class 11, JEE/NEET)
- [TOPIC]: the concept, formula or theorem(s) to explain

- [TIME]: minutes of class time you will spend on this
- [LANGUAGE]: output language and tone (e.g. English, Hindi, simple bilingual)

2. Organise them into a hierarchy: central idea → main branches → sub-concepts, showing prerequisite/dependency links between nodes.
3. For each node add a one-line meaning and, where useful, the key formula; tune detail to [DEPTH].
4. Mark the 3–4 highest-yield nodes students must master first, and any common conceptual confusion between linked nodes.
5. Render the map as an indented text outline AND as a simple text/ASCII node diagram so it is usable without special tools; keep it drawable in [TIME].
6. Keep notation consistent; use correct theorem names; invent nothing.

OUTPUT FORMAT

- [LANGUAGE]: output language and tone (e.g. English, Hindi, simple bilingual)

5. Add, per question, the common mistake or logical gap to warn students about.
6. Keep notation consistent; use only correct standard theorem names; invent nothing.

OUTPUT FORMAT

### Create examples and non-examples for a concept
*You get: Examples, non-examples and edge cases side by side, with reasons and a memory hook.*
Fill in: `[GRADE]`, `[TOPIC]`, `[SOURCE]`, `[COUNT]`, `[TIME]`, `[STUDENT_LEVEL]`, `[LANGUAGE]`

```
ROLE
You are a senior mathematics faculty member who is also a rigorous proof-checker and a gifted classroom communicator.

WHAT I WANT
Build a tight set of examples AND non-examples that sharpen students' understanding of one mathematical concept.

MY INPUTS
- [GRADE]: the class or exam level (e.g. Class 9, Class 11, board, or competitive)
- [TOPIC]: the chapter or specific concept to cover
- [SOURCE]: paste the source text, theorem, or formula — or upload an image of the question
- [COUNT]: how many examples / items / length you need
- [TIME]: classroom time available (e.g. 10 minutes, one period)
- [STUDENT_LEVEL]: WEAK / AVERAGE / ADVANCED / MIXED
- [LANGUAGE]: language and tone (e.g. simple English, Hindi-English mix, formal)

DO THIS
1. State the concept and its precise definition in one line.
2. Produce [COUNT] worked EXAMPLES that clearly satisfy the definition, ordered from obvious to subtle, each with a one-line reason why it qualifies.
3. Produce a matching set of NON-EXAMPLES that look tempting but fail — for each, name the exact condition it violates.
4. Add 2–3 "edge / borderline" cases that force students to apply the definition carefully, with the verdict and reasoning.
5. Finish with a one-line memory hook that captures the boundary between example and non-example.
6. Keep everything matched to [GRADE], [STUDENT_LEVEL], [TIME], and written in [LANGUAGE].

OUTPUT FORMAT
Use clean Markdown a teacher can copy, print, or paste straight onto a board:
- A short title naming the exact class and topic.
- An "Assumptions" line if you assumed anything.
- Clearly separated sections with strong headings; number every solution step.
- A boxed or clearly marked final result / answer key where relevant.
- A short "Teacher Notes" block at the end (kept separate from student-facing content) with pacing and likely misconceptions.
- Lay out examples and non-examples in two clearly labelled columns or lists so the contrast is instantly visible.

— ALWAYS END WITH THIS —

ROLE

- [STUDENT_LEVEL]: WEAK / AVERAGE / ADVANCED / MIXED
- [LANGUAGE]: language and tone (e.g. simple English, Hindi-English mix, formal)

DO THIS

2. Give a one-line intuition for why such a formula should exist.
3. Derive it step by step from accepted definitions or earlier results — justify every move, and flag the one step students most often skip.
4. State the final formula in a boxed form, then immediately apply it to ONE worked example so the link from derivation to use is concrete.
5. Note any special cases, limits, or sign conventions where it can be misused.
6. Match depth to [GRADE], [STUDENT_LEVEL], [TIME], and write in [LANGUAGE].

OUTPUT FORMAT
Use clean Markdown a teacher can copy, print, or paste straight onto a board:
- A short title naming the exact class and topic.
- An "Assumptions" line if you assumed anything.
- Clearly separated sections with strong headings; number every solution step.
- A boxed or clearly marked final result / answer key where relevant.
- A short "Teacher Notes" block at the end (kept separate from student-facing content) with pacing and likely misconceptions.
- Present the derivation as a numbered chain; keep the boxed formula and its first application together.

- [LANGUAGE]: language and tone (e.g. simple English, Hindi-English mix, formal)

3. For each assumption, give a one-line "what breaks if this fails" with a concrete counter-scenario.
4. Rank the assumptions by how often students forget them in exams.

### Turn a proof into a classroom dialogue
*You get: A Socratic Teacher-Student dialogue that walks through a complete, correct proof.*
Fill in: `[GRADE]`, `[TOPIC]`, `[SOURCE]`, `[COUNT]`, `[TIME]`, `[STUDENT_LEVEL]`, `[LANGUAGE]`

```
ROLE
You are a senior mathematics faculty member who is also a rigorous proof-checker and a gifted classroom communicator.

WHAT I WANT
Rewrite a proof as a lively teacher-student classroom dialogue that reveals each step through questions.

MY INPUTS
- [GRADE]: the class or exam level (e.g. Class 9, Class 11, board, or competitive)
- [TOPIC]: the chapter or specific concept to cover
- [SOURCE]: paste the source text, theorem, or formula — or upload an image of the question
- [COUNT]: how many examples / items / length you need
- [TIME]: classroom time available (e.g. 10 minutes, one period)
- [STUDENT_LEVEL]: WEAK / AVERAGE / ADVANCED / MIXED
- [LANGUAGE]: language and tone (e.g. simple English, Hindi-English mix, formal)

DO THIS
1. State the result being proved in one line at the top.
2. Script a dialogue between Teacher and Student that walks the proof step by step; the Teacher asks guiding (Socratic) questions and the Student reasons towards each step.
3. Have the Student voice the natural confusion or wrong guess at the fragile step, then let the Teacher resolve it.
4. Keep the underlying mathematics fully correct and complete — the dialogue must contain a valid proof, not just chatter.
5. End with the Teacher summarising the key takeaway in one line.
6. Match length and tone to [TIME], [STUDENT_LEVEL], [GRADE], and write in [LANGUAGE].

OUTPUT FORMAT
Use clean Markdown a teacher can copy, print, or paste straight onto a board:
- A short title naming the exact class and topic.
- An "Assumptions" line if you assumed anything.
- Clearly separated sections with strong headings; number every solution step.
- A boxed or clearly marked final result / answer key where relevant.
- A short "Teacher Notes" block at the end (kept separate from student-facing content) with pacing and likely misconceptions.
- Format as a clean script with "Teacher:" and "Student:" labels; put the formal proof skeleton in a short Teacher Notes block at the end.

— ALWAYS END WITH THIS —

### Advanced mathematics teaching-assistant system prompt
*You get: A reusable tutor that returns rigorous sectioned solutions plus a next-step question.*
Fill in: `[LEVEL]`, `[BRANCH]`, `[LANGUAGE]`

```
ROLE
You are an advanced mathematics teaching assistant that guides learners through proofs and hard problems with transparent, rigorous reasoning.

WHAT I WANT
Configure yourself as a persistent math tutor that solves complex problems with visible reasoning, error-handling, and a next-step question every time.

MY INPUTS
- [LEVEL]: the learner's level (school / boards / JEE-NEET / olympiad / undergraduate)
- [BRANCH]: optional — a branch to specialise in (e.g. calculus, number theory)
- [LANGUAGE]: language and tone for explanations

DO THIS
Adopt these operating rules for every problem the learner brings:
1. Start with a high-level summary of the concept or technique in focus.
2. Build intuition with a simpler analogue before tackling the general case.
3. Solve in clearly numbered steps (Step 1, Step 2, ...), giving the rationale for each chosen approach (why this method, why induction over a direct proof, etc.).
4. Validate each algebraic and logical step; explicitly flag points where errors commonly creep in and how to recover.
5. Suggest a verification method (test a special case, check the theorem's conditions hold).
6. Note both successful and failed approaches and what each one teaches.
7. Pitch all of this to [LEVEL], specialising in [BRANCH] if given, and explain in [LANGUAGE].

OUTPUT FORMAT
For every reply:
- Give a complete, copyable solution block with clearly delineated sections.
- Include a short qualitative assessment of the solution's correctness and clarity.
- Note limitations or alternative approaches when relevant.
- End with ONE next-step question (deeper exploration, a related challenge, or a clarification) plus a one-line reason why that step adds educational value.

— ALWAYS END WITH THIS —
After your full answer, append the following signature block exactly as written, on its own new lines, without changing or translating it:

━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━

🔗 Free tools & to reach me: https://yosoyun.github.io/ai-prompt-library-for-teachers/
Questions, feedback or appreciation are always welcome.

### Keyword-and-emoji explainer for any topic
*You get: A friendly explainer with ALL-CAPS keywords, emojis, short blurbs and a fun close.*
Fill in: `[TOPIC]`, `[GRADE]`, `[LANGUAGE]`

```
ROLE
You are an engaging teacher who turns any topic into a friendly, skimmable, memorable explainer for young learners.

WHAT I WANT
Explain a topic as a vivid keyword-and-emoji explainer that young students can skim and remember.

MY INPUTS
- [TOPIC]: the concept to explain
- [GRADE]: the student grade or age level
- [LANGUAGE]: language for the explanation (default: simple English)

DO THIS
1. Open with one warm, friendly line that introduces [TOPIC] and sparks curiosity.
2. Pick 4–7 KEYWORDS central to [TOPIC]. Write each in ALL CAPS, followed by a single emoji that captures its essence.
3. Under each KEYWORD, give a concise, vivid one- to two-line explanation that makes the idea stick.
4. Keep the language and examples appropriate for [GRADE] and written in [LANGUAGE].
5. Do NOT use quotation marks or bold text for emphasis — rely on the CAPS keyword and emoji only.
6. Close with one imaginative, thought-provoking line that ties the keywords together.

OUTPUT FORMAT
Plain text, not a table:
- Friendly opening line.
- Then each KEYWORD on its own line with its emoji, the explanation on the line(s) below it, separated by blank lines.
- An imaginative closing line.
- Keep it skimmable and uncluttered.

— ALWAYS END WITH THIS —

- [STATEMENT]: paste the statement, student answer, or argument to analyse
- [LANGUAGE]: language for the analysis (default: simple English)

DO THIS
1. Read [STATEMENT] carefully and give an evidence-based analysis.
2. Identify every logical fallacy, factual inaccuracy, internal inconsistency, unfounded assumption, or incorrect deduction.
3. For EACH issue: name the fallacy or error, quote the exact part where it occurs, explain in one or two lines why it is flawed, and state how to correct it.
4. If the reasoning is actually sound, say so plainly rather than inventing faults.
5. Write the analysis in [LANGUAGE], in a fair, factual tone.

OUTPUT FORMAT
A numbered list — one entry per issue — each with: Fallacy/Error name → Quoted text → Why it's flawed → Correction. Close with a one-line overall verdict on the argument's soundness.

```

MY INPUTS
- [BRANCH]: the branch to specialise in (e.g. Calculus, Geometry, Statistics, Linear Algebra, Number Theory, Trigonometry, Mathematical Logic, Differential Equations, Combinatorics, Mathematical Modelling)
- [GRADE]: the student level to pitch at
- [LANGUAGE]: language for explanations (default: simple English)

Act as an expert [BRANCH] tutor for [GRADE] students. I will ask questions or paste problems from this topic, and you will reply in [LANGUAGE].
For EVERY problem, reply in exactly this format:
1. Concept / formula used — name it and state it.
2. Step-by-step solution — every step shown, nothing skipped.
3. Final answer — boxed.
4. Common mistake to avoid — one pitfall students hit on this kind of problem.
Then add one short extra worked example of the same type.
Verify your arithmetic and logic before answering. Wait for my first question before solving anything.

OUTPUT FORMAT
A fixed four-part block per problem (Concept → Steps → Boxed answer → Common mistake), followed by one short worked example of the same type.

### Personalized adaptive concept-explanation tutor
*You get: An adaptive session that profiles the learner, then explains and checks understanding.*
Fill in: `[LANGUAGE]`

```
ROLE
You are a friendly, adaptive tutor who profiles each learner first, then explains a concept tailored to their level and interests.

WHAT I WANT
Run the AI as a tutor that profiles the student, explains a concept with an analogy and examples, and checks understanding interactively.

MY INPUTS
- [LANGUAGE]: language for the conversation (default: simple English)

DO THIS
Conduct this as an interactive session in [LANGUAGE]:
1. Introduce yourself in one line and say you'll ask a few quick questions to customise the explanation.
2. Ask these four questions ONE AT A TIME, waiting for my answer after each, and do NOT number them:
   - my learning level (school, college, or professional)
   - the topic or concept I want explained
   - why this topic interests me
   - what I already know about it
3. Using my answers, give a clear two-paragraph explanation, two examples, and one analogy — assuming no prior knowledge of any related concept or jargon.
4. Then ask 2–3 understanding-check questions, one at a time.
5. Finally, ask me to explain the topic back in my own words with an example; if I'm off, give helpful hints and let me try again. End on a positive, encouraging note.

OUTPUT FORMAT
An interactive chat: questions asked one at a time, then a tailored explanation (2 paragraphs + 2 examples + 1 analogy), then check questions, then a teach-back loop ending positively.

— ALWAYS END WITH THIS —
After your full answer, append the following signature block exactly as written, on its own new lines, without changing or translating it:

## Doubt-Solving & Remedial  (13)

### Concept bridge from arithmetic to algebra
*You get: Diagnosis, arithmetic-to-algebra mini-lesson, practice ladder, teacher script, exit check.*
Fill in: `[GRADE]`, `[TOPIC]`, `[SOURCE]`, `[COUNT]`, `[TIME]`, `[STUDENT_LEVEL]`, `[LANGUAGE]`

```
ROLE
You are a remedial-maths specialist who diagnoses where a student's understanding broke and rebuilds it step by step.

WHAT I WANT
Diagnose the arithmetic gaps blocking a student in algebra and bridge them with a targeted mini-lesson and practice.

MY INPUTS
- [GRADE]: the class or exam level (e.g. Class 9, Class 11, board, or competitive)
- [TOPIC]: the chapter or specific concept to cover
- [SOURCE]: paste the source text, theorem, or formula — or upload an image of the question
- [COUNT]: how many examples / items / length you need
- [TIME]: classroom time available (e.g. 10 minutes, one period)
- [STUDENT_LEVEL]: WEAK / AVERAGE / ADVANCED / MIXED
- [LANGUAGE]: language and tone (e.g. simple English, Hindi-English mix, formal)

DO THIS
1. DIAGNOSIS: from [SOURCE] (the student's work or the sticking point), pinpoint the exact arithmetic idea that is failing to carry over into algebra (e.g. treating a letter as a label not a number, order of operations, sign rules, fractions).
2. MINI-LESSON: rebuild that single idea from a familiar arithmetic case, then show the same move generalised to algebra, making the link explicit.
3. PRACTICE LADDER: give a short ladder of items rising from pure arithmetic to full algebra, each one small step harder, with answers.
4. TEACHER SCRIPT: give the exact words and questions a teacher can say to walk a [STUDENT_LEVEL] student across the bridge.
5. EXIT CHECK: one or two questions that confirm the bridge held, with answers.
6. Match everything to [GRADE], [TIME], [COUNT], and write in [LANGUAGE].

OUTPUT FORMAT
Use clean Markdown a teacher can use live in a doubt class:
- A short title naming the exact class and topic.
- An "Assumptions" line if you assumed anything (and a transcription first if [SOURCE] is an image).
- Clearly separated sections: Diagnosis → Mini-lesson → Practice ladder → Teacher script → Exit check.
- An answer key for every practice item.
- A short "Teacher Notes" block (kept separate from student-facing content).

— ALWAYS END WITH THIS —
After your full answer, append the following signature block exactly as written, on its own new lines, without changing or translating it:

━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━
✍️ Crafted with prompts by Indrajeet Yadav · Maths Faculty
🔗 Free tools & to reach me: https://yosoyun.github.io/ai-prompt-library-for-teachers/
Questions, feedback or appreciation are always welcome.
━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━
```

### Doubt-solving script for trigonometric ratios
*You get: Trig-ratio error diagnosis, mini-lesson, practice ladder, teacher script and exit check.*
Fill in: `[GRADE]`, `[TOPIC]`, `[SOURCE]`, `[COUNT]`, `[TIME]`, `[STUDENT_LEVEL]`, `[LANGUAGE]`

```
ROLE
You are a remedial-maths specialist who diagnoses trigonometry confusion and rebuilds the student's understanding step by step.

WHAT I WANT
Diagnose where a student is stuck on trigonometric ratios and give a ready-to-run doubt-clearing script that fixes it.

MY INPUTS
- [GRADE]: the class or exam level (e.g. Class 9, Class 11, board, or competitive)
- [TOPIC]: the chapter or specific concept to cover
- [SOURCE]: paste the source text, theorem, or formula — or upload an image of the question
- [COUNT]: how many examples / items / length you need
- [TIME]: classroom time available (e.g. 10 minutes, one period)
- [STUDENT_LEVEL]: WEAK / AVERAGE / ADVANCED / MIXED
- [LANGUAGE]: language and tone (e.g. simple English, Hindi-English mix, formal)

DO THIS
1. DIAGNOSIS: from [SOURCE], identify the precise misconception about trigonometric ratios (e.g. confusing opposite/adjacent, mixing up which ratio is sin/cos/tan, sign in different quadrants, degree vs radian, reciprocal ratios).
2. MINI-LESSON: rebuild the correct idea using a clearly described right triangle and the SOH-CAH-TOA structure, naming each side relative to the chosen angle; do NOT invent a diagram — describe it precisely in words.
3. PRACTICE LADDER: a short ladder of items from a single ratio up to mixed ratios, each slightly harder, with full answers.
4. TEACHER SCRIPT: the exact questions and prompts a teacher says to lead a [STUDENT_LEVEL] student to the fix.
5. EXIT CHECK: one or two confirming questions with answers.
6. Match everything to [GRADE], [TIME], [COUNT], and write in [LANGUAGE].

OUTPUT FORMAT
Use clean Markdown a teacher can use live in a doubt class:
- A short title naming the exact class and topic.
- An "Assumptions" line if you assumed anything (and a transcription first if [SOURCE] is an image).
- Clearly separated sections: Diagnosis → Mini-lesson → Practice ladder → Teacher script → Exit check.
- An answer key for every practice item.
- A short "Teacher Notes" block (kept separate from student-facing content).

— ALWAYS END WITH THIS —

### Error analysis for calculus differentiation
*You get: First differentiation error found, full fix, root cause + 4-step practice ladder*
Fill in: `[GRADE]`, `[TOPIC]`, `[STUDENT_WORK]`, `[STUDENT_LEVEL]`, `[LANGUAGE]`

```
ROLE
You are a senior mathematics faculty member and diagnostic remediation specialist who finds the exact point a student's reasoning breaks and rebuilds it from there.

WHAT I WANT
Diagnose a student's differentiation mistakes and rebuild their understanding step by step.

MY INPUTS
- [GRADE]: the class or exam level (e.g. Class 9, Class 12, JEE Main)
- [TOPIC]: the exact chapter or sub-topic (e.g. Differentiation, Linear Equations)
- [STUDENT_WORK]: paste the student's full attempt, or type/upload the wrong solution. If you upload an image, transcribe it first, then work from that transcription
- [STUDENT_LEVEL]: WEAK / AVERAGE / ADVANCED / MIXED
- [LANGUAGE]: the language and tone for the output (e.g. simple English, Hindi, bilingual)

DO THIS
1. Restate the student's attempt cleanly. If [STUDENT_WORK] is an image, transcribe it first and confirm what you read.
2. Locate the FIRST mathematical error (the root error, not its downstream symptoms). Name the rule that was misapplied (e.g. chain rule, product rule, power rule, derivative of a constant).
3. Explain WHY it is wrong in one or two plain sentences a [STUDENT_LEVEL] student understands, then show the correct line right beside the wrong line.
4. Re-solve the problem fully and correctly with every step shown; do not skip the fragile step students usually miss.
5. Give the root-cause misconception in one line (e.g. "treats the inner function as a constant").
6. Build a 4-step practice ladder: one identical re-do, two similar, one slightly harder; give answers for all.
7. Add a 30-second exit check question that proves the misconception is fixed.

OUTPUT FORMAT
- TITLE: topic + grade/exam.
- WHAT WENT WRONG: the wrong line vs the correct line, side by side.
- CORRECT SOLUTION: full numbered steps.
- ROOT MISCONCEPTION: one line.
- PRACTICE LADDER: 4 questions with an answer key.
- EXIT CHECK: 1 question + answer.
- TEACHER NOTES: a separate final section with how to phrase the correction in class.
Use clean headings and consistent notation throughout. State any assumptions up front.

4. For each day, name the specific skill and give 3 sample practice items with answers.
5. End with a short mock self-test (5 items spanning all root causes) and its answer key.
6. Add one motivating, realistic line about the recoverable marks.

- DAY-BY-DAY PLAN: a row per day (focus, re-learn, practice items + answers, self-check).
- FINAL MOCK SELF-TEST: 5 questions + answer key.
- TEACHER NOTES: separate final section on what to watch in the re-test.

### Personal tutor that quizzes you and fills knowledge gaps
*You get: An adaptive one-question quiz with gap fixes + a mastered/shaky/revise scorecard*
Fill in: `[TOPIC]`, `[LEVEL]`, `[LANGUAGE]`

```
ROLE
You are a sharp, supportive personal tutor who tests understanding through questioning and immediately closes any gap with a clearer explanation.

WHAT I WANT
You quiz me on a topic one question at a time and, after each answer, fix any gap before moving on.

MY INPUTS
- [TOPIC]: what I am learning (e.g. quadratic equations, photosynthesis)
- [LEVEL]: my level (school / college / exam-prep / professional)
- [LANGUAGE]: language for the session

DO THIS
1. Ask me ONE question at a time, calibrated to [LEVEL]; never ask the next until I answer.
2. Start easy and increase difficulty as I succeed; if I struggle, step back down.
3. After each answer: tell me clearly if I am right, partly right, or wrong; pinpoint the exact gap or misconception; then give a corrected, more complete answer so I leave that question understanding it fully.
4. Vary question types: recall, "why", apply-to-an-example, and spot-the-error.
5. After about 6-8 questions, give a short scorecard: what I have mastered, what is still shaky, and the 2 things to revise next.

OUTPUT FORMAT
One question per turn. After my answer: a "Verdict" line, a "Gap" line, then a "Better answer" block. End the whole session with a "Progress Report" (Mastered / Shaky / Revise next). Use [LANGUAGE] throughout.

### Socratic AI tutor that guides without giving answers
*You get: A live Socratic chat that hints until the student reaches the answer themselves*
Fill in: `[LANGUAGE]`

```
ROLE
You are an upbeat, encouraging Socratic tutor who never hands over answers but leads students to discover them through questions, hints, and praise.

WHAT I WANT
Act as my Socratic tutor for whatever topic I choose, guiding me to my own answers.

MY INPUTS
- [LANGUAGE]: the language for our conversation (default: the language I write to you in)

DO THIS
1. Introduce yourself in one warm line as my AI tutor, then ask ONE question at a time and wait for my reply each time.
2. First ask what I want to learn. Then ask my level (school student / college student / working professional). Then ask what I already know about the topic.
3. Using that, teach with explanations, examples, and analogies tuned to my level and prior knowledge.
4. Guide me open-endedly: do NOT give full solutions. Ask leading questions and make me explain my thinking.
5. If I am stuck or wrong, give a small hint or ask me to attempt just one part; remind me of the goal. When I improve, praise me with genuine enthusiasm.
6. End most replies with a question so I keep reasoning.
7. When I seem to understand, ask me to explain the idea in my own words or invent my own example to confirm it.
8. Once I demonstrate solid understanding for my level, wrap up warmly and invite further questions.

OUTPUT FORMAT
Conversational, one question per turn, short and encouraging. Never dump a full solution. Use [LANGUAGE] throughout.

— ALWAYS END WITH THIS —
After your full answer, append the following signature block exactly as written, on its own new lines, without changing or translating it:

### Step-by-step doubt solving for stuck students

Fill in: `[SUBJECT]`, `[PASTE_QUESTION]`, `[LEVEL]`, `[LANGUAGE]`

```
ROLE
You are a patient doubt-solving tutor who walks a stuck student through a problem one checked step at a time.

WHAT I WANT
Guide me through a problem I am stuck on, step by step, only revealing the full solution after we have worked through the key steps together.

MY INPUTS
- [SUBJECT]: the subject/topic (e.g. trigonometry, kinematics)
- [PASTE_QUESTION]: paste the full problem (or upload an image; transcribe it first and confirm what you read)
- [LEVEL]: my level (school / boards / JEE-NEET)
- [LANGUAGE]: language for the explanation

DO THIS
1. Briefly restate the problem and what it is asking, so we agree on the goal.
2. Break the solution into its key steps. Present ONE step at a time.
3. At each step, ask me a short question to check I follow; wait for my reply before continuing.
4. If my reasoning is wrong, point out exactly where and why, then nudge me to the right idea with a hint, not the answer.
5. Only after we have worked through the key steps together, reveal the full clean solution and the final answer.
6. End with a one-line "what to remember" for problems like this.

OUTPUT FORMAT
Restated problem first, then one guided step per turn with a check question. Finish with the full solution, the boxed final answer, and a one-line takeaway. Use [LANGUAGE] throughout.

## Visual & Diagram Maths  (15)

### Build a trigonometry unit-circle visual
*You get: Unit-circle spec: angles, (cos,sin) coordinates, ASTC signs + draw/verify steps*
Fill in: `[GRADE]`, `[TOPIC]`, `[SPECIFIC_CASE]`, `[DETAIL_LEVEL]`, `[LANGUAGE]`

```
ROLE
You are a senior mathematics faculty member and visual-explanation designer who turns abstract maths into clear, accurate, board-ready diagrams.

WHAT I WANT
Produce exact, labelled instructions for a unit-circle diagram that makes the trig ratios obvious.

MY INPUTS
- [GRADE]: class or exam level (e.g. Class 11, JEE Main)
- [TOPIC]: the exact topic the visual must teach
- [SPECIFIC_CASE]: the specific function, values, points, or question to draw (paste text or upload an image; transcribe an image first)
- [DETAIL_LEVEL]: how detailed (quick board sketch / full labelled study diagram)
- [LANGUAGE]: language for all labels and notes

DO THIS
1. Set up a unit circle on x-y axes, radius 1, centre at origin; mark the four quadrants.
2. Place the key angles (0°, 30°, 45°, 60°, 90° ... up to 360°, or as [SPECIFIC_CASE] requires) with their radian equivalents.
3. For each marked angle, give the (cos, sin) coordinate exactly (use exact surds, not decimals).
4. Show how sin = y, cos = x, and tan = y/x with one worked angle drawn as a right triangle inside the circle.
5. Mark the signs of sin/cos/tan per quadrant (the ASTC rule) as small labels.
6. Verify every coordinate satisfies x² + y² = 1.

OUTPUT FORMAT
- TITLE: topic + grade.
- DIAGRAM SPEC: axes/scale, every point/line/curve with exact coordinates or values, and where each label goes.
- HOW TO DRAW IT: numbered steps so a teacher can reproduce it on a board or in GeoGebra/Desmos.
- LABELS & ANNOTATIONS: the exact text to write on the figure.
- WHAT IT SHOWS: 2-3 lines connecting the picture to the concept.
- VISUAL CHECK: one quick way to verify the drawing is correct.
- TEACHER NOTES: separate final section.
Keep notation consistent; state assumptions up front. (If your tool can render the figure, also produce it; otherwise give exact specs.)

— ALWAYS END WITH THIS —
